INTR ODUCTION A dv ances in the capability of ar tificial intellig ence (AI) are br inging about ne w human- AI interaction modes in the engineer - ing design process, lar g el y shifting from discrete deleg ation of tasks to iterativ e collaboration. In AI-assis ted w orkflo w s, AI sy s- tems often g enerate sugg es tions that designers mus t assess and decide whether to accept, reject or modify [1]. An e x ample is the g enerativ e compute r -a ided design (C AD) w orkflo w : design- ers receiv e AI-g enerated design alter nativ es in rapid succession, compressing traditionall y multi-s tep processes (e.g. ideation and v er ification) into a single e v aluation [2, 3]. In this ne w conte xt of repeated human- AI interaction (HAI), appropr iate reliance decisions (e.g., accept, reject, and modify) are cr ucial f or successful collaboration. U nder -reliance is cos tl y ; ignor ing helpful AI sugg es tions means missing high-per f or ming alter nativ es and spending e xtra time and resources e xplor ing de- signs the AI could ha v e sur f aced ear l y [4]. Ov er -reliance can also be e xpensiv e and e v en hazardous; fla w ed designs can car r y do wns tream conseq uences f or anal y sis, prototyping, manuf actur - ing, and deplo yment. F or e x ample, if an engine er accepts an AI- g enerated topology that o v er looks latent f ailure modes, the result ma y be late-s tag e redesign, scrapped prototypes, or unsaf e field per f or mance [5]. Theref ore, it is impor tant that d esigners ' per - ceiv ed capability of an AI sy s tem aligns with the sy s tem' s actual per f or mance, a concept that is coined as tr us t calibration [6, 7]. T o suppor t tr us t calibration, man y human-computer interac- tion (HCI) researc hers, including those specificall y in HAI, ha v e e xplored inter f ace mec hanisms to communicate model reliability to users, suc h as uncer tainty visualizations and calibrated confi- dence disclosures [8 10]. While these mec hanisms can impro v e reliability judgments, the y often increase cognitiv e load par ticu- lar l y in time-sensitiv e settings [9, 11, 12]. High cognitiv e load pushes users to w ard simplified heur is tics that leads to ine ectiv e decision-making [13, 14], lea ving the mis-reliance issue unre- sol v ed. An alter nativ e approac h uses adaptiv e inter v entions that prompt users when the y appear to o v er -rel y or under -rel y on AI. Ex amples include sur f acing e xplanations, slo wing interactions, and tailored suppor t to the user ' s cur rent tr us t s tate [15 19]. While promising, these methods often treat tr us t as an unob- ser v ed latent s tate and req uire real-time detection of user tr us t, whic h is a capability that is not full y realized y et. R ealizing suc h real-time prediction req uires unders tanding ho w tr us t in AI e v ol v es o v er repeated interactions. Y et e xis ting w orks in this do- main o er limited c haracter ization of tr us t dynamics: whether c hang es are g radual or abr upt, symmetr ic or asymmetr ic to posi- tiv e and ne g ativ e f eedbac k, or dominated b y recent tr ials or long er his tor y [20, 21]. A clearer temporal descr iption is needed bef ore real-time tr us t prediction becomes f easible. T o address this g ap, Chong et al. (2022) proposed a compu- tational model of tw o cons tr ucts that shape AI tr us t and reliance decisions o v er time [22]: confidence in AI and self-confidence. While these cons tr ucts do not capture the full breadth and com- ple xity of tr us t, the y align with tw o ma jor antecedents empha- sized in pr ior tr us t researc h: perceiv ed ability of the tr us tee and the tr us tor ' s propensity or willingness to rel y [23]. Confidence in AI reflects ho w capable users think the AI is f or a giv en task, while self-confidence moderates willingness to accept e xter nal assis tance. U nders tanding ho w these cons tr ucts e v ol v e across interactions can inf or m real-time tr us t prediction and adaptiv e inter v ention design. Although Chong et al.' s model pro vides a useful f ounda- tion [22], tw o limitations con s train its applicability to broader engineer ing design conte xts and be y ond. F irs t, the model treats reliance decisions as binar y (accep t/reject), neglecting more com- ple x beha viors suc h as par tial adoption and modification. Second, it sho w s lo w er predictiv e accuracy f or self-confidence, sugg es ting that the self-confidence update mec hanism remains insu cientl y captured. T o address these limitations, w e ref or mulate the model b y implementing the f ollo wing f our c hang es: 1. an modular update sk eleton that introduces momentum into confidence updating, 2. an e xpanded e xper ience encoding that captures modifica- tion decision, 3. an accumulated e xpectation mec hanism dr iv en b y predic- tion er ror , and 4. an asymmetr ic parameter ization of slo w lear ning be- tw een self-confidence and confidence in AI c hannels with alignment-sensitiv e amplification. W e then e v aluate whether and ho w this ref or mulation impro v es the model' s ability to reproduce empir ical confidence tra jector ies f or both cons tr ucts with an AI-assis ted c hess task dataset [24]. While the c hess task is not a design task, this datase t is c hosen f or its a v ailability and resemblance to v ar ious AI-assis ted design tasks. The dataset includes human- AI interaction data, suc h as AI sugg es tions, reliance decisions, and f eedbac k, o v er multiple tr ials, whic h can be f ound in iterativ e AI-assis ted design tasks. F ur ther more, this dataset is used to e v aluate Chong et al.' s model [22], pro viding a good ref erence f or compar ing the per f or mance of the ref or mulated model. The e v aluation results sho w that the ref or mulation subs tantiall y impro v es predictiv e accuracy , espe- ciall y f or the self-confidence c hannel. 2. REL A TED W ORK 2.1. Human-AI Collabor ation in Engineering Design Engineer ing design increasingl y in v ol v es iterativ e human- AI collaboration, where AI acts as a g enerativ e par tner rather than a bac k -end optimizer . A frame w ork f or human- AI teaming in engineer ing design dis tinguishes multiple integ ration modalities, from passiv e tools in v ok ed on demand to proactiv e par tners and process manag ers that guide w orkflo w [25]. As AI mo v es be y ond its role as a tool, AI-assis ted design often in v ol v es AI proposing candidate ar tif acts or design directions, then designers cr itiq uing, s teer ing, and re vising them o v er multiple cy cles. V ar ious empir ical s tudies illus trate the impact of this shift on team w ork and design process and outcomes. In recent drone de- sign e xper iments, h ybr id teams with AI ag ents sho w ed impro v ed coordination, broader e xploration, and s trong er adaptation to dis- r uptions than human-onl y teams [1], and an AI process man- ag er matc hed human manag ers in shaping team problem-sol ving beha vior [26]. Ho w e v er , adding a high-per f or ming AI par tner does not consis tentl y impro v e design outcomes. Zhang et al. (2021) f ound that high-per f or ming teams w ere hindered while lo w -per f or ming teams initiall y benefited b y a high-per f or ming AI teammate, indicating that AI e ects depend on the e xis ting team dynamic [27]. When AI ag ents are proactiv e teammates, the collaboration sometimes depends more on ho w humans adapt their communication than on the AI' s capabilities. [28]. These findings sugg es t that design outcomes are jointl y pro- duced b y human and AI contr ibutions, making credit and blame di cult to assign to a single actor . tend to blame themsel v es e v en f or neg ativ e outcomes caused b y their AI par tner [29]. This attr ibution ambiguity is a defining f eature of collaborativ e design w orkflo w s: the same outcome ma y be attr ibuted to AI capability , human skill, or their inter - action, leading to di erent updates in belief s about the AI and the self [4, 30, 31]. Pr ior w ork suppor ts this dual-belief vie w , sho wing that confidence in AI responded pr imar il y to poor AI per f or mance, whereas self-confidence w as sensitiv e to c hang es in AI accuracy rather than to the le v el of accuracy itself [29]. These findings motiv ate modeling the belief s in self and AI in paral- lel to accuratel y unders tand credit/blame attr ibution patter ns in AI-assis ted decision-making and the associated design outcomes. 2.2. T rust Calibr ation in AI-Assist ed Decision Making T r us t calibration, defined as aligning reliance with actual sy s tem capability , is central to pre v enting misuse (o v er -reliance) and disuse (under -reliance) of automation [32]. Mos t calibration researc h has f ocused on pro viding users with inf or mation to sup- por t their judgment of AI advice, suc h as uncer tainty displa y s, confidence scores, or other e xplanations. Suc h cues can shift reliance beha vior , though their e ects v ar y with task conte xt and user goals [7, 33]. P ar t of this v ar iability ma y also s tem from ho w users inter pret e vidence, penalizing algor ithms more hea vil y after er rors than re w arding them after successes, contr ibuting to algor ithm a v ersion [34]. Calibration theref ore depends not onl y on what e vidence is presented, but also on ho w that e vidence is processed o v er time. Another popular approac h to calibrating tr us t is beha vioral inter v entions, detecting when a user appears to o v er -rel y or under - rel y on AI and activ el y adjus ting the interaction. Some e x amples include req uir ing independent jus tification, slo wing acceptance, or modulating suppor t intensity [15, 16, 18, 19]. These inter - v entions req uire real-time inf erence of the user ' s latent tr us t s tate from obser v able beha vior . Ho w e v er , this inf erence has not been su cientl y realized, giv en the di culty of captur ing the dynamic and multi-f aceted tr us t updating mec hanism. In engineer ing design, this real-time tr us t detection is es- peciall y c hallenging. Muc h of the e xis ting calibration literature assumes that e vidence about sy s tem per f or mance is relativ el y in- ter pretable, so that users can judg e whether the success or f ailure should be credited to AI. In design w orkflo w s, ho w e v er , outcomes are often jointl y produced through sugg es tion, cr itiq ue, and re- vision, w eak ening the applicability of this assumption. T r us t calibration in suc h settings depends not onl y on designers ' judg- ments of AI competence but also on their perceptions of their o wn contr ibution to the joint outcome, req uir ing models that trac k both of these belief s o v er time. 2.3. Modeling T rust Dynamics Computational modeling e or ts of tr us t and confidence can be or g anized along tw o ax es: temporal resolution (s tatic v s. dy - namic) and belief s tr ucture (single-belief v s. multi-belief ) [32, 35 37]. S tatic approac hes treat tr us t as a s table attitude assessed via sur v e y s or pos t-hoc judgments. The y tend to be limited in e xplaining tr ial-to-tr ial fluctuations in repeated human- AI in- teractions [38]. In contras t, dynamic models commonl y rep- resent tr us t as a latent s tate updated through e xper ience. X u and Dudek (2015) used online Ba y esian inf erence to es timate a single tr us t v ar iable from obser v ed beha vior in human-robot col- laboration [39]. Hu et al. (2019) proposed an er ror -cor rection f or mulation in whic h tr us t in automation updates tr ial-b y -tr ial as a function of e xper ience, cumulativ e tr us t, and e xpectation bias [40]. While these models can capture temporal dynamics of tr us t, the y often simplify tr us t as a single-belief sy s tem. Ho w e v er , a single-belief approac h lik el y cannot accuratel y predict tr us t and subseq uent reliance decisions, as the y depend on both perceiv ed sy s tem (i.e., AI) capability and self confidence [23, 41]. Subseq uent w orks introduced multi-belief models of tr us t. Chong et al. (2022) e xtended Hu et al.' s er ror -cor rection model to tw o c hannels, confidence in AI and self-confidence, updated in parallel with c hannel-specific parameters [22, 40]. W illiams et al. (2023) modeled the same tw o belief s as coupled s tates in a par - tiall y obser v able Mark o v decision process, captur ing their proba- bilis tic relationship with reliance [37]. Both models es tablish that reliance is shaped jointl y b y confidence in AI and self-confidence. W illiams et al.' s discrete s tate categor ies (high/lo w) limit contin- uous tra jector y prediction, while Chong et al.' s f or mulation en- ables tr ial-b y -tr ial prediction under a simpler reliance s tr ucture. Theref ore, this w ork builds on Chong et al.' s dual-c hannel model, introducing ne w mec hanisms to impro v e its alignment with find- ings from cognitiv e science and its applicability to AI-assis ted design w orkflo w s. 3. Model Fitting W e confir m the per f or mance of the baseline model b y repli- cating the model fitting result presented b y Chong et al. [22]. F or eac h confidence c hannel, the optimal model parameters f U 4  U 0  U 1  l 1  l 2  l 3  l 4  W g are es timated independentl y f or eac h c hannel b y minimizing leas t-sq uares er ror betw een predicted and repor ted confidence o v er all tes t tr ials. DISCUSSION The ref or mulated model impro v es predictiv e accuracy across both confidence c hannels, with the lar g es t g ains in self-confidence (adjus ted ' 2 = 0.424 to 0.632). Be y ond accuracy , the model' s representation of confidence dynamics in human AI collabora- tion is better aligned with psy c hology , confidence in AI and self- confidence e v ol ving separatel y through their o wn update mec h- anisms. The ref or mulation also impro v es the model' s applica- bility to human- AI design collaboration scenar ios b y captur ing a broader rang e of interaction patter ns. 6.1. T o w ards Confidence-a w ar e Human-AI Int er action in Design The ref or mulated model has implications f or ho w AI-assis ted design inter f aces detect and respond to user confidence s tates. W e highlight three aspects: source-specific diagnosis of miscalibra- tion, the design r isk posed b y alignment amplification, and ho w these mec hanisms ma y c hang e in engineer ing design w orkflo w s. 6.1.1. Source-specific diagnosis. By separatel y es timat- ing confidence in AI, self-confidence, and their update sensitiv - ities, the model can identify both miscalibration and its lik el y source. Lo w reliance on AI ma y reflect jus tified dis tr us t, inflated self-confidence, or both. Rapid acceptance of AI sugg es tions ma y reflect lo w self-confidence or ag reement-sensitiv e o v er -updating. This dis tinction matters f or inter v ention design. If the user ap- pears o v er l y confident in their o wn judgment but sk eptical of the AI, the inter f ace could pro vide s trong er e vidence f or the AI recommendation, suc h as calibrated reliability cues, uncer tainty inf or mation, or per f or mance his tor y [7, 9]. If the user appears inclined to tr us t the AI while lac king confidence in their o wn judgment, the inter f ace could slo w acceptance b y req uir ing an initial independent response [18], side-b y -side compar ison, or br ief jus tification bef ore commitment [16]. Compared with a sin- gle global tr us t es timate, the dual-c hannel model suppor ts more tar g eted calibration. 6.1.2. Alignment as a design-r ele v ant signal. The fitted model sugg es ts that alignment e v ents dispropor tionatel y amplify self-confidence, with subs tantial v ar iation across par ticipants. V ar iance decomposition of alignment-tr ial prediction er ror sup- por ts this inter pretation: in the AI c hannel, betw een-tr ial v ar iance e x ceeds betw een-par ticipant v ar iance, and the patter n re v erses f or self-confidence, indicating that the self-confidence g ain from alignment is dispersed across individuals rather than concentrated in specific tr ials. One possible reason is that alignment is easier to inter pret in the AI c hannel than in the self c hannel. F or confidence in AI, ag reement signals local compatibility betw een the user ' s c hoice and the AI recommendation. F or self-confidence, the same e v ent ma y be read either as competence confir mation ( I identified a s trong mo v e ) or as v alidation of AI reliance ( AI guided me ) [4, 57, 58]. This ambiguity is consis tent with the heterog eneity captured b y 6 align , although the present s tudy does not tes t that mec hanism directl y . Because the e ect v ar ies b y person rather than b y tr ial con- te xt, it cannot be manag ed simpl y b y controlling when alignment inf or mation is presented. F or inter f ace design, this raises a concer n: e xplicitl y signaling ag reement betw een the user and the AI ma y increase self-confidence without impro ving decision accuracy [57]. More broadl y , con v er g ence ma y be better framed as one cue among man y rather than as v alidation [33]. 6.1.3. Gener alization t o eng ineering design. The c hess task shares common c haracter is tics with AI-assis ted engineer ing design tasks, allo wing this ref or mulated model and the associated insights from this w ork to be applicable to v ar ious design scenar - ios. Both setting in v ol v e repeated e v aluation of AI sugg es tions and reliance decisions. In both settings, users repeatedl y e v alu- ate AI sugg es tions, mak e reliance decisions, and f or m judgments about both the AI' s and their o wn capability . Both scenar ios also in v ol v e ambiguous credit assignment betw een human and AI contr ibutions. These parallels mak e the c hess task an appro- pr iatel y controlled tes tbed in whic h the model' s core mec hanisms can be isolated and v alidated. Designers dur ing an AI-assis ted engineer ing design task are lik el y to displa y similar confidence mec hanisms with the parameters adjus ted f or the specific task. The par tial w eight assignment parameter d is especiall y salient in engineer ing design. In design scenar ios, modification is lik el y the dominant interaction mode [30, 43], so confidence up- dates will need to accuratel y reflect human- AI joint contr ibution. Rather than doing an e xhaus tiv e sw eep of d v alues, additional e vidence can help separate those contr ibutions to deter mine the appropr iate d v alue. Pr ior design researc h has de v eloped metr ics f or compar ing g eometr ic ar tif acts through g eometr ic similar ity , f eature o v er lap, or cons traint div er g ence [59, 60]. These measures ma y be utilized to q uantify the deg ree of modification betw een an AI sugg es tion and the final design. In this w a y , the d v alues can be obser v able and car r y g reater e xplanator y v alue to confidence updates. A similar e xtension applies to alignment. In c hess, alignment appears as a discrete coincidence: the AI happens to recommend the mo v e the user already identified. In design, con v er g ence ma y emer g e g raduall y across edits, dis tr ibuting the amplification e ect across multiple edits. When AI adapts to the user through fine-tuning or personalization [61], this con v er g ence becomes more freq uent and meaningful. U nder these conditions, the 6 align component ma y be eng ag ed more freq uentl y , compounding self- confidence amplification in a w a y that reflects collaboration fit rather than competence. Momentum ( V : ) ma y lik e wise pla y a lar g er role in design. In the c hess dataset, tr ials are independent and confidence is repor ted betw een tr ials, resulting in coarse, discrete updates that limit the continuity of confidence tra jector ies across tr ials. By contras t, engineer ing design often in v ol v es temporall y e xtended interac- tions, where confidence de v elops o v er seq uences of proposals, re visions, and e v aluations. U nder this conditions, momentum ma y become more prominent, making confidence update more path-dependent. In that sense, the timing of cor rectiv e inter v en- tion is more conseq uential. 6.2. Limit ations and F utur e W ork Se v eral limitations of the present s tudy sugg es t directions f or future w ork. F irs t, the par tial w eight assignment parameter d f or modify tr ials is fix ed rather than fitted. This is appropr iate f or the present dataset, where the modify tr ials are sparse. Ho w e v er , in r ic her datasets, d ma y become more tractable b y treating d as a s tandard global fitted parameter . F ur ther more, because d is modification-specific, it ma y be better inf or med b y ar tif act- le v el e vidence of the e xtent of modification, as e xplained in the pre vious section. Second, the e xper ience signal assumes binar y outcome f eed- bac k (positiv e/neg ativ e). In engineer ing design, outcome q uality is typicall y e v aluated along multiple dimensions, suc h as saf ety f actor or maximum s train from FEA anal y sis. F eedbac k is there- f ore often presented as a per f or mance score rather than a simple success-or -f ailure signal. Theref ore, the discrete f eedbac k and e xper ience types could be replaced with a continuous encoding. More nuanced f eedbac k can c hang e ho w s trongl y people update their belief s [44], pro viding useful insight f or the model. Third, the model assumes that all update parameters are s tationar y within a user . In long er design w orkflo w s, a user ' s sensitivity to f eedbac k, alignment amplification, and momentum ma y c hang e as the user becomes more f amiliar with the task. 10 Cop yr ight © 2026 b y ASME

A ccommodating time-v ar ying parameters w ould increase model fle xibility , while potentiall y increasing the r isk of o v er fitting. Theref ore, a careful regular ization or hierarc hical es timation of time-v ar ying parameters could impro v e the model fur ther . F inall y , the interaction betw een the tw o confidence c hannels and its mapping to reliance decisions remains une xplored. C ON CL USION This w ork proposes a ref or mulated dual-c hannel confidence model, predicting confidence in AI and self-confidence dur ing AI-assis ted design settings. From Chong et al.' s baseline model, the ref or mulation includes a ne w ph y sics-inspired f or m that ac- counts f or momentum of confidence c hang e, an e xpanded inter - action encoding with modification decision, a redefined accumu- lated e xpectation ter m, asymmetr ic slo w lear ning across c han- nels, and alignment amplification. T og ether , the ref or mulated model impro v es the prediction accuracy in both c hannels (AI and self ), with the lar g es t g ain in self-confidence. The model' s fit is adjus ted ' 2 = 0.792 in the AI c hann el and adjus ted ' 2 = 0.632 in the self c hannel. This model sugg es ts a pathw a y from la- tent confidence dynamics to confidence detection and subseq uent adaptiv e inter v entions in human- AI design w orkflo w s.
